    *   Regarding "environment variable": The text says "add the `--application-namespaces` parameter to the container's startup command". It does not mention enabling it via an environment variable.
    *   Therefore, the statement claims it can be done via a container parameter **OR** an environment variable. The text supports container parameter (command line argument).     *   More importantly, the statement specifies the "Argo CD repository server component".         2.  `argocd-application-controller` (reconciles apps)
        3.  `argocd-repository-server` (not explicitly detailed in this specific text for *this* feature, though part of the stack).

The text doesn't explicitly call it an environment variable.
    *   Crucially, the text says "add the `--application-namespaces` parameter".
    *   The component name "repository server" is likely the dealbreaker. The text refers to `argocd-server`. In Argo CD architecture, the `argocd-server` is the Application Server.     So the statement is False.

From the "Implementation details" section:
"In order for an application to be managed and reconciled outside the Argo CD's control plane namespace, two prerequisites must match:
1. The `Application`'s namespace must be explicitly enabled using the `--application-namespaces` parameter for the `argocd-application-controller` and `argocd-server` workloads. This parameter controls the list of namespaces that Argo CD will be allowed to source `Application` resources from globally. Any namespace not configured here cannot be used from any `AppProject`.
1. The `AppProject` referenced by the `.spec.project` field of the `Application` must have the namespace listed in its `.spec.sourceNamespaces` field. This setting will determine whether an `Application` may use a certain `AppProject`."

So there are **two** prerequisites:
1. Configure `--application-namespaces` on the workloads.
2. Configure `sourceNamespaces` in the `AppProject`.

The statement claims "the only thing that is required is to add the namespace '--application-namespaces' parameter".
This ignores the second requirement regarding the `AppProject`'s `sourceNamespaces`.

Therefore, the statement is False.

The text says: "In order for an application to be managed and reconciled outside the Argo CD's control plane namespace, two prerequisites must match".
This confirms there are two things, not just one.
The statement says "the only thing that is required".
So the statement is False.

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/user-guide/app_deletion/' -> kubectl delete with no finalizer | labels:  [simple multiple-choice] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m The following is an Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
[2;1m>[22;22m kind: Application
[2;1m>[22;22m metadata:
[2;1m>[22;22m   name: jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m   namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m spec:
[2;1m>[22;22m   destination:
[2;1m>[22;22m     namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m     server: https://kubernetes.default.svc
[2;1m>[22;22m   project: default
[2;1m>[22;22m   source:
[2;1m>[22;22m     path: kustomize-guestbook
[2;1m>[22;22m     repoURL: https://github.com/argoproj/argocd-example-apps
[2;1m>[22;22m     targetRevision: master
[2;1m>[22;22m   syncPolicy:
[2;1m>[22;22m     automated:
[2;1m>[22;22m       prune: true
[2;1m>[22;22m       selfHeal: true
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m The Application is Synced and Healthy, and it is being used to deploy a number of resources to the cluster.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m A user issues the following command:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl delete -n jgw application/jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- The user wants to know what happens when a `jgw-app` Argo CD Application is deleted from the cluster using `kubectl delete -n jgw application/jgw-app`.

The application has a sync policy that is `automated: { prune: true, selfHeal: true }`.
The application is currently `Synced` and `Healthy`.

The key question is whether the deletion of the Argo CD Application resource itself triggers a cascade deletion of the resources managed by that Application (the "child resources" like Deployments, Services, etc.) when using `kubectl delete`.

Looking at the reference material provided:

1.  **Deletion Using `kubectl`**:
    *   "To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset and then delete the app".
    *   "To perform a cascade delete set the finalizer... `kubectl delete app APPNAME`".
    *   Default behavior for cascading deletion: `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io`.
    *   "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
    *   "The default propagation policy for cascading deletion is foreground cascading deletion."

2.  **Default Behaviour**:
    *   The metadata section in the provided kubectl command reference implies there's a default finalizer behavior.
    *   Under "About The Deletion Finalizer": "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
    *   "The default propagation policy for cascading deletion is [foreground cascading deletion](https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/architecture/garbage-collection/#foreground-deletion)."

3.  **Implicit assumptions**:
    *   When a standard Kubernetes resource (like an Argo CD Application) is created by default in this context (especially with the reference material provided which emphasizes the finalizer mechanism), does `kubectl delete` automatically trigger the finalizer logic or require manual patching?
    *   The reference material says: "When you invoke `argocd app delete` with `--cascade`, the finalizer is added automatically."
    *   However, it also says under "About The Deletion Finalizer": "The default behaviour is foreground cascading deletion". This implies the finalizer exists by default on the resource.
    *   The command used is `kubectl delete -n jgw application/jgw-app`. This is a raw kubectl delete command.
    *   If the finalizer `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` is present on the Application object (which the text says is the "default behaviour"), then deleting the resource with `kubectl delete` triggers K8s garbage collection. Since the finalizer waits for Argo CD controller to finish, the Argo CD controller handles the cascade deletion of the resources.

Reasoning:
- The user wants to know what happens to the resources deployed by an Argo CD Application when a user executes `kubectl delete -n jgw application/jgw-app`.

1.  **Analyze the input Application object:**
    *   `metadata` contains `finalizers`.
    *   One of the finalizers is `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io`.
    *   This is the default finalizer for Argo CD Applications.

2.  **Analyze the command:**
    *   `kubectl delete -n jgw application/jgw-app`
    *   This command attempts to delete the `Application` resource named `jgw-app` in the `jgw` namespace using the standard Kubernetes deletion mechanism.

3.  **Analyze the behavior of Kubernetes Finalizers (based on the reference material):**
    *   The reference material section "About The Deletion Finalizer" states: "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
    *   It also states: "The default propagation policy for cascading deletion is [foreground cascading deletion]."
    *   Crucially, under "Deletion Using `kubectl`", it says: "To perform a cascade delete set the finalizer, e.g. using `kubectl patch`... To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset and then delete the app".
    *   However, the provided `Application` YAML explicitly has the finalizer `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` already set in `metadata`.
    *   When `kubectl delete` is run on a resource that has a finalizer attached, Kubernetes starts the deletion process but pauses the resource removal until the finalizer is handled.
    *   Until the finalizer is removed, the resource cannot be deleted.
    *   The Itemplate "The default behaviour is foreground cascading deletion" applies here.
    *   Therefore, since the finalizer is present, Argo CD's controller will intercept this deletion request.
    *   Argo CD will be notified (via events or controller logic) that this Application is being deleted.
    *   It will trigger a "cascade delete", which means it will delete the managed resources (child resources like Deployments, Services, etc.) within the target namespace (`jgw`).
    *   Once the managed resources are deleted, Argo CD removes the finalizer, allowing Kubernetes to fully remove the Application itself.

4.  **Evaluate the Options:**
    *   **A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.**
        *   This aligns with the "foreground cascading deletion" default described in the material. The finalizer triggers the controller to clean up child resources before deleting the App resource.
    *   **B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.**
        *   This describes a non-cascade delete (finalizer removed beforehand or `--cascade=false` equivalent). Since the finalizer is present by default, this is not what happens with a standard `kubectl delete`.
    *   **C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.**
        *   Argo CD manages resources recursively (e.g., manifests in `kustomize-guestbook` path). It deletes all resources managed by the application, not just immediate children (though technically "all child resources" usually implies all reconciled objects). Option A covers this better than C, which implies a distinction between "immediate" and deeper resources that isn't standard behavior (it's usually all managed resources).
    *   **D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.**
        *   Incorrect. The Application *will* be deleted (sequentially), but only after child resources are cleaned up due to the foreground deletion policy tied to the finalizer.

5.  **Confirming with Reference Material:**
    *   "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
    *   "The default propagation policy for cascading deletion is [foreground cascading deletion]."
    *   "Foreground... Deletes the application and all its managed resources... Waits for all managed resources to be deleted before the Application is removed."
    *   Since the YAML shows the finalizer exists (`resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io`), the standard `kubectl delete` command will trigger this logic (Kubernetes starts deletion -> Finalizer exists -> Controller invoked -> Resources deleted -> Finalizer removed -> App deleted).
    *   Therefore, both the Application and its managed resources (child resources) are deleted.

6.  **Conclusion:** Option A is the correct answer.

    *   So `kubectl delete` acts as a trigger for the finalizer process.
    *   Result: Application is deleted *after* resources are deleted (Foreground). Effectively, everything is deleted.

[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m

[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)

- The user wants to know the outcome of the command `argocd app delete jgw-app --cascade=false` on the resources deployed by the Argo CD application.

1.  **Analyze the command:**
    *   `argocd app delete`: Specifies the application to delete.
    *   `jgw-app`: The name of the application.
    *   `--cascade=false`: This is a flag specifically designed to control the deletion behavior regarding child resources.

2.  **Analyze the reference material:**
    *   Under "## Deletion Using `argocd`":
        *   "To perform a non-cascade delete: `argocd app delete APPNAME --cascade=false`"
        *   Under "Deletion Options (Propagation Policies)":
            *   "### 3. Non-Cascading (Orphan)"
            *   "Deletes **only** the Application resource"
            *   "All managed resources (Deployments, Services, ConfigMaps, etc.) are **preserved** in the cluster"
            *   "The finalizer is removed automatically before deletion"

3.  **Synthesize the findings:**
    *   The flag `--cascade=false` explicitly triggers a "Non-Cascading" delete.
    *   The reference material states this deletes only the Application resource itself.
    *   It explicitly states that managed resources are preserved.
    *   Therefore, the child resources (.Deployments, Services, etc.) are NOT deleted.

4.  **Evaluate the options:**
    *   A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted. (Incorrect, this is `--cascade=true` or default).
    *   B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted. (Correct, matches "non-cascade" behavior).
    *   C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted. (Incorrect, non-cascade deletes nothing).
    *   D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted. (Incorrect, the Application itself is deleted in both cascade and non-cascade scenarios, the difference is the resources).

5.  **Conclusion:** The correct answer is B.

[2;1m>[22;22m The following is an Argo CD Application:

[2;1m>[22;22m   namespace: jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m   finalizers:
[2;1m>[22;22m     - resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io
[2;1m>[22;22m spec:
[2;1m>[22;22m   destination:

[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m The Application is Synced and Healthy, and it is being used to deploy a number of resources to the cluster.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m A user issues the following commands:
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl patch app jgw-app -n jgw -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": null}}' --type merge
[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl delete app jgw-app
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- The user wants to know what happens when a specific Argo CD Application is deleted using `kubectl` commands provided in the question.

1.  **Analyze the Application and the commands:**
    *   Application Name: `jgw-app`
    *   Namespace: `jgw`
    *   Initial state: The application has a finalizer `resources-finalizer.argoproj.io` (default foreground cascading deletion).
    *   Command 1: `kubectl patch app jgw-app -n jgw -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": null}}' --type merge`
        *   This removes the finalizer from the metadata.
    *   Command 2: `kubectl delete app jgw-app`
        *   This initiates the deletion of the Application resource itself.

2.  **Understand Argo CD deletion logic based on reference material:**
    *   **Finalizer:** The reference material explicitly states: "The default propagation policy for cascading deletion is foreground cascading deletion... When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
    *   **Removing Finalizer:** The reference material section "Deletion Using `kubectl`" states: "To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset and then delete the app."
    *   **Non-Cascade Delete:** The material quotes the definition of Non-Cascading (Orphan) deletion: "Deletes only the Application resource. All managed resources... are preserved in the cluster." It also mentions: "The finalizer is removed automatically before deletion [when selecting Non-Cascading]."
    *   **The Specific Sequence:** The user manually patches the finalizer to `null` *before* deleting. This forces the deletion to be non-cascading (or orphan).
    *   **Mechanism:** Without the finalizer `resources-finalizer.argoproj.io`, Argo CD's application controller will not see the deletion in progress and will not interfere to clean up the resources. Kubernetes standard garbage collection for the Application resource will proceed immediately. However, Argo CD normally prevents deletion of the App until it finishes deleting resources (enforced by the finalizer).
    *   **Result:** By removing the finalizer, the App is deleted. Since the finalizer that triggers the cleanup of the child resources is gone, Argo CD *does not* perform the cleanup of the deployed resources (Deployments, Services, etc.).
    *   **Conclusion:** The Application is deleted, but the child resources remain in the cluster.

3.  **Evaluate the Options:**
    *   A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted. (Incorrect, this happens if the finalizer is present).
    *   B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted. (Correct, this describes the non-cascade/orphan deletion achieved by removing the finalizer).
    *   C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted. (Incorrect, Argo CD manages the full set of resources from its manifest, not just "immediate" children, and removing the finalizer stops cleanup).
    *   D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted. (Incorrect, the App resource itself is deleted by `kubectl delete` once the finalizer is stripped).

4.  **Confirm with Reference Material:**
    *   Section "Deletion Using `kubectl`": "To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset and then delete the app". This matches the commands exactly.
    *   Section "3. Non-Cascading (Orphan)": "Deletes only the Application resource. All managed resources... are preserved".

    Therefore, the Application is deleted, resources are kept.

    Wait, check the exact question text again.
    "What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application"
    The options describe the state of the Application vs child resources.
    Option B: "The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted."

    Let's double-check the logic.
    If finalizer is present -> Argo CD cleans up resources then deletes App.
    If finalizer is removed -> App is deleted by K8s immediately. Argo CD doesn't know to clean up because the trigger (finalizer) is gone. The resources stay running (managed by K8s now).

    The reference material says:
    "If you only want to remove the Application resource but keep the deployed workloads, use Non-Cascading delete... The finalizer is removed automatically before deletion."
    Here, the user *manually* removed the finalizer to force this behavior effectively.

    So, B is the correct answer.

5.  **Final check:**
    *   Command: `kubectl patch ... -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": null}}'` -> Removes finalizer.
    *   Command: `kubectl delete app jgw-app` -> Deletes the App object.
    *   Reference: "To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset and then delete the app." ... "Deletes only the Application resource. All managed resources... are preserved".
    *   Outcome: App deleted, resources (child resources) remain.
    *   Choice: B.

    Wait, one nuance: Does "child resources" mean *all* child resources defined in the source? Yes, in Argo CD context, "resources deployed via the Application" are the managed resources. Without the finalizer, Argo CD does not re-apply the deletion logic to them. So they persist.

    Answer is B.

[2;1m>[22;22m kubectl delete app jgw-app -n jgw
[2;1m>[22;22m ```
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What happens to the resources that were deployed via the Argo CD Application:
[2;1m>[22;22m A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- The user wants to know the outcome of the following sequence of commands:
1. `kubectl patch app jgw-app -n jgw -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": ["resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io"]}}' --type merge`
2. `kubectl delete app jgw-app -n jgw`

Based on the reference material provided.

**Analysis:**
1.  **Initial State**: The Application `jgw-app` is already Synced and Healthy.
2.  **Command 1 (Patch)**: The command adds the finalizer `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` to the Application metadata.
3.  **Command 2 (Delete)**: The command attempts to delete the Application `jgw-app`.
4.  **Reference Material**:
    *   Section "Deletion Using `kubectl`":
        *   "To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset..."
        *   "To perform a cascade delete set the finalizer, e.g. using `kubectl patch`:" -> `kubectl patch app APPNAME -p '{"metadata": {"finalizers": ["resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io"]}}' --type merge` followed by `kubectl delete app APPNAME`.
    *   Section "About The Deletion Finalizer":
        *   "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
        *   "The default propagation policy for cascading deletion is foreground cascading deletion."
6.  **Outcome**: By setting the finalizer and then deleting, the user is explicitly triggering a cascading delete (as indicated in the reference material under "Deletion Using kubectl"). The finalizer prevents Kubernetes from deleting the App object immediately. Argo CD observes the deletion request, sees the finalizer, and understands that this is a request for handling resource cleanup (cascading deletion). Consequently, Argo CD deletes the child resources associated with this Application before the Application object itself is removed.

**Evaluating Options:**
*   A) The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted. (Matches "cascading delete" description).
*   B) The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted. (Matches "Non-Cascading" behavior, which requires *not* having the finalizer).
*   C) The Application is deleted, but only the immediate child resources of the Application are deleted. (Argo CD cascading delete typically targets all resources managed by the app, not just immediate children, but "all child resources" covers the broader scope better than "immediate"). However, the key distinction is between deleting resources vs keeping them. Option A aligns best with the definition of cascade delete provided in the text ("deletes both the app and its resources").
*   D) The Application is not deleted, because the child resources are not deleted. (Incorrect).

**Conclusion**: The commands specified are the exact sequence for performing a cascade delete using `kubectl`. Setting the finalizer tells Argo CD to handle deletion, and does not explicitly handle deletion. Wait, technically, the finalizer stops the *Kubernetes API server* from deleting the object immediately. Argo CD waits on this finalizer. When the App deletion request hits, Argo CD's controller manages the finalizer logic. The reference text says: "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources." and "To perform a cascade delete set the finalizer...".

Therefore, the result is that both the Application and its managed resources are deleted.

Option A says "The Application and all child resources of the Application are deleted."

Option B says "The Application is deleted, but the child resources of the Application are not deleted."

The distinction is Cascade (Resources Deleted) vs Non-Cascade (Resources Kept). The presence of the finalizer `resources-finalizer.argocd.argoproj.io` indicates Cascade Delete.

Therefore, Option A is the correct answer.

Double check:
Reference: "To perform a cascade delete set the finalizer... kubectl delete app APPNAME". Result implied: Resources are deleted.
Reference: "When deleting an Application with this finalizer, the Argo CD application controller will perform a cascading delete of the Application's resources."
Reference: "Foreground cascading deletion... Deletes the application and all its managed resources".

The commands set up exactly the condition for cascading delete.

Final Answer seems to be A.

One small nuance in Option C: "only the immediate child resources". Since Kustomize usually generates resources directly (DaemonSets, Deployments, Services, etc.) and not sub-applications (unless explicitly referenced), "all child resources" in Option A is the standard definition of Application resource deletion vs the resource tree/node in Parent-Child pattern. The text says: "Deletes the application and all managed resources". Option A says "all child resources of the Application". This is semantically equivalent in the context of Kubernetes objects managed by the App.

Let's verify Option A vs B vs C.
A: App + all child resources deleted.
B: App deleted, resources kept.
C: App deleted, immediate child resources deleted.

Given "cascading delete... deletes the application and all its managed resources", Option A is the most accurate description of a full cascade delete. Option C implies a limited scope which isn't standard for this deletion command.

The reference explicitly states: "To perform a cascade delete set the finalizer... kubectl delete app APPNAME". If the goal was to keep resources (B), the finalizer should not be present (reference says "To perform a non-cascade delete, make sure the finalizer is unset...").

Therefore, the finalizer causes the resources to be deleted.

Answer is A.

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/core_concepts/' -> refresh | labels:  [simple] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m What Argo CD concept does this describe: When this is triggered, the latest resource state in Git is compared with the live state. determines what is different (but don't necessarily act on it just yet)
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer.
[2;1m>[22;22m The answer is 1 word.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- Thinking Process:

1.  **Analyze the Request:**
    *   Question: What Argo CD concept does this describe?
    *   Description: "When this is triggered, the latest resource state in Git is compared with the live state. determines what is different (but don't necessarily act on it just yet)"
    *   Constraint: Provide ONLY the answer.
    *   Constraint: The answer is 1 word.
    *   Reference Material: Provided a list of Argo CD Core Concepts (Application, Application source type, Target state, Live state, Sync status, Sync, Sync operation status, Refresh, Health, Tool, Configuration management tool, Configuration management plugin).

2.  **Evaluate the Description against Reference Material:**
    *   Description key points:
        *   Triggered.
        *   Compare latest resource state in Git with live state.
        *   Determines what is different.
        *   Do *not* necessarily act on it just yet (comparison/assessment only, not sync/update).

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/user-guide/directory/' -> directory-type Argo CD app will read yaml and JSON only | labels:  [simple multiple-choice] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m A directory-type Argo CD Application will read plain manifest files contained within the git repository. Which file types will be interpreted as Kubernetes manifests?
[2;1m>[22;22m A) .yml, .yaml
[2;1m>[22;22m B) .yml, .yaml, .json
[2;1m>[22;22m C) .yml, .yaml, .json, kustomize
[2;1m>[22;22m D) .yml, .yaml, .json, kustomize, .jsonnet
[2;1m>[22;22m E) None of the above
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- The user wants to know which file types are interpreted as Kubernetes manifests by a directory-type Argo CD Application based on the provided reference material.

1.  **Analyze the Reference Material:**
    *   Under the section "Directory", it states: "A directory-type application loads plain manifest files from `.yml`, `.yaml`, and `.json` files."
    *   Under the warning section: "Directory-type applications only work for plain manifest files. If Argo CD encounters Kustomize, Helm, or Jsonnet files when directory: is set, it will fail to render the manifests."
    *   Later sections discuss including/excluding files and skipping rendering, but the core definition of what files are loaded as plain manifests is in the first paragraph of the "Directory" section.

2.  **Evaluate the Options:**
    *   A) `.yml`, `.yaml`: The text explicitly mentions `.yml`, `.yaml`, and `.json`. So this is incomplete.
    *   B) `.yml`, `.yaml`, `.json`: This matches the text exactly ("A directory-type application loads plain manifest files from `.yml`, `.yaml`, and `.json` files.").
    *   C) `.yml`, `.yaml`, `.json`, `kustomize`: The warning explicitly says "If Argo CD encounters Kustomize... when directory: is set, it will fail to render the manifests." So `kustomize` is not interpreted as a plain manifest in a directory-type app.
    *   D) `.yml`, `.yaml`, `.json`, `kustomize`, `.jsonnet`: Similarly, `.jsonnet` is excluded in the warning ("...Helm, or Jsonnet files... it will fail to render").
    *   E) None of the above: Since B matches the text, this is incorrect.

3.  **Conclusion:** The text clearly states `.yml`, `.yaml`, and `.json` are the plain manifest files loaded. Kustomize, Helm, and Jsonnet are handled differently and cause failure in directory-type applications.

4.  **Final Selection:** Option B.

5.  **Constraint Check:** "Provide ONLY the answer. The answer will be a single letter from the multiple-choice list. Don't write any other text."

    Answer: B

[2;1m>[22;22m We are defining an Argo CD Application, and deploying plain manifests from a directory defined within a Git repository (a directory-type Argo CD Application).
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m However, at present, in our Argo CD Application, Argo CD is deploying files with types ".yaml", ".yml", and ".json".
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m I want to exclude Argo CD from deploying "*.json" files defined within that directory, while still continuing to deploy "*.yaml" and "*.yml".
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What field can we set in the Argo CD Application resource, in order to tell Argo CD to avoid deploying "*.json" files?
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Specify only the name/value of the field. For example: "spec.source.directory.(key): (value)" (without quotes). Include BOTH the key and the value.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- The user wants to know which field in an Argo CD Application resource can be set to exclude files matching the pattern "*.json" from being deployed when using a directory-type application.

Looking at the reference material provided:

1. There's a section called "Including/Excluding Files"
2. Under "Excluding Certain Files", it shows that you can exclude files using the `exclude` option within the `directory` configuration
3. The example shows:
   ```yaml
   spec:
     source:
       directory:
         exclude: '{config.json,env-usw2/*}'
         include: '*.yaml'
   ```

So the field is `spec.source.directory.exclude` with the value being the glob pattern.

The user wants to exclude "*.json" files specifically.

The question asks for "the name/value of the field" in the format "spec.source.directory.(key): (value)".

For excluding "*.json" files:
- Field: spec.source.directory.exclude
- Value: '*.json' (or "*.json" in YAML syntax)

Let me check the format requested: "Specify only the name/value of the field. For example: "spec.source.directory.(key): (value)" (without quotes)"

So I should provide:
spec.source.directory.exclude: '*.json'

Or should I include quotes in the value? The example shows that for include patterns they mention it's important to quote so the shell doesn't expand. In YAML, strings are typically quoted. Let me look at the reference material again.

In the YAML examples, they don't show quotes around the values in the exclude field examples:
```yaml
spec:
  source:
    directory:
      exclude: '{config.json,env-usw2/*}'
      include: '*.yaml'
```

So the pattern doesn't need quotes within the YAML value, but the star is a special character in many shells. In YAML context, '*.json' would be written as is or with single quotes if needed. The actual value should be '*.json' (inside single or double quotes in shell, but in YAML manifest, you can just have the string literal).
 
For the YAML resource, the value should be `'*.json'` with quotes to represent it as a string. The example pattern shows epochs and directories without additional wrapping beyond the glob pattern itself, so I should follow that convention.

Looking at the reference material's shell example, they use single quotes to prevent shell expansion: `--directory-exclude "config.yaml"`. In the YAML documentation, patterns like `'.yaml'` or `'*.yaml'` are shown without shell escaping needed.

The simplest correct answer becomes:
spec.source.directory.exclude: '*.json'

This matches YAML string syntax where the single quotes don't escape anythingâ€”they just denote a string literal.

[ tests from 'https://argo-cd.readthedocs.io/en/stable/user-guide/sync-options/' -> spec.syncPolicy.syncOptions[ApplyOutOfSyncOnly=true] can be used to enable selective sync | labels:  [simple] ]

[2;1m>[22;22m I am using Argo CD to deploy resources to my kubernetes cluster.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m I am deploying thousands of objects, which means it can take a long time for Argo CD to sync all those objects (and also puts pressure on API server).
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m What is the name of the Argo CD sync option that I can add to Application's 'spec.syncPolicy.syncOptions' field, to ensure that Argo CD only attempts to sync resources that are out of sync?
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m Provide ONLY the answer. The answer is the name and value of the sync policy to add. Dont quote the answer or use markdown.
[2;1m>[22;22m 
[2;1m>[22;22m 
> (reference text)
Reasoning:
- The user is asking about an Argo CD sync option that ensures only out-of-sync resources are synced, particularly useful when deploying thousands of objects to reduce load on the API server.

Looking at the reference material, I need to find the sync option related to syncing only out-of-sync resources.

From the reference material:

## Apply Resources OutOfSync Only

"The default behavior when syncing your application is to apply every object in the application.
For applications containing thousands of objects, this takes quite a long time and puts undue pressure on the Kubernetes API server. It will also significantly increase the size of the `status.operationState.syncResult.resources` field, which may impact the Kubernetes database.

Turning on the sync option will sync only out-of-sync resources.

Unlike [Selective Sync](./selective_sync.md), when `ApplyOutOfSyncOnly` is enabled, Sync Hooks will still run and the sync will be recorded in the history."

The example shows:
```yaml
apiVersion: argoproj.io/v1alpha1
kind: Application
spec:
  syncPolicy:
    syncOptions:
      - ApplyOutOfSyncOnly=true
```

So the answer is: ApplyOutOfSyncOnly=true

The user wants ONLY the answer with no quotes, no markdown.


A: [33mapplyoutofsynconly=true[0m
- Expected: [34mapplyoutofsynconly=true[0m
  Match: applyoutofsynconly=true
- [32;1mPASS[0;22m
